Local News

The Commercial Consolidation Committee Convened Fellow Trade Association Representatives Yesterday 115

General Meeting of Trade Association Representatives

The Shanghai Special Municipality Merchant Groups Consolidation Committee convened a general meeting of members' representatives from various industries at 9:00 AM yesterday to elect the first executive and supervisory committee members of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and discuss various important cases. Over two hundred representatives from the Central Party Headquarters and other entities, as well as member representatives, attended. The speeches of the representatives and the names of the elected executive and supervisory committee members are recorded below.

Meeting Order (1) Ring bell to start the meeting, (2) Presidium and all representatives take their seats, (3) Play music (Zhabei Charity Troupe Military Band), (4) All stand at attention, (5) Sing the Party song, (6) Bow three times to the Party flag, national flag, and the portrait of the Premier, (7) Read the Premier's last will and testament respectfully, (8) Observe three minutes of silence, (9) Opening remarks (Wang Xiaolai), (10) Report (Wang Yansong), (11) Admonitory speech by the representative of the Party Headquarters, (12) Admonitory speech by the representative of the government, (13) Speeches by guests, (14) Announce the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce charter, (15) Elect the first executive committee members and alternate executive committee members of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, (16) Report the list of elected executive committee members and alternate executive committee members, (17) Elect the first supervisory committee members and alternate supervisory committee members of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, (18) Report the list of elected supervisory committee members and alternate supervisory committee members, (19) Discuss proposals, (20) Closing remarks, (21) Take a photograph, (22) Play music and adjourn the meeting.

Participating Representatives Yu Wenxian, representative of the Central Party Headquarters; (Pan Gongzhan, representing) the National Government; Zhao Jinqing, representative of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce; Tao Baichuan, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters; Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce; Pan Gongzhan, representative of the Municipal Government; Song Zhengqing and Sheng Juncai of the Social Affairs Bureau; Xiong Shi of the Wusong Garrison Command;

Hui (Chen Yuxiang, representing); Xu Junde, representative of the Director of the Municipal Finance Bureau; Huang Guangdou, representative of the Municipal Public Security Bureau; and two hundred and several tens of member representatives, etc.

Meeting Staff Presidium: Wang Yansong, Wang Xiaolai, Ye Huijun, Xu Jilu, Qin Runqing; Master of Ceremonies: Lu Fengzhu; Recorders: Nie Desheng, Zhou Zixun; Ushers: Hu Xisheng, Zheng Chengqing, Lu Wenshao, Chen Songyuan; Thirty people including Wu Zhihao and others were publicly elected as vote counters, and all staff members served as receptionists.

Meeting Proceedings After the ceremonial procedures were completed, Wang Xiaolai of the presidium first delivered the opening remarks. Next, representatives of the Party Headquarters and the government gave admonitory speeches, and guests gave speeches. After that, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce charter was discussed. Then, the election of the first executive and supervisory committee members and alternate executive and supervisory committee members began. Finally, the proposals submitted by various industry associations were discussed. Xu Jilu of the presidium delivered the closing remarks, and the meeting adjourned at 8:00 PM.

Chairman's Speech Chairman Wang Xiaolai delivered the opening remarks, saying: The reasons for convening this general meeting of trade association representatives today have already been stated in detail in the application to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and have been published in the local newspapers. I believe everyone has already seen it. However, according to the usual meeting order, there is an item for opening remarks, so I will briefly reiterate. Originally, this committee was ordered to be established in May of last year. According to Article 15 of the organizational outline prescribed by the central government, "The Commercial Consolidation Committee shall be abolished when the unified organization is established after the promulgation of the unified organization laws and regulations." Therefore, from this point of view, this committee is a preparatory committee for unifying merchant organizations, or, to put it simply, a preparatory committee for the "Shanghai Chamber of Commerce." However, the planned consolidation period of this committee was originally thought to be a few months or half a year. Why has it taken more than a year to prepare? There are several reasons for this. First, the laws and regulations promulgated by the central government require a great deal of review and consideration. The Chamber of Commerce Law was promulgated on August 15, 1929, the implementing regulations for the Chamber of Commerce Law were promulgated on November 13, and the implementing regulations for the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law were promulgated on January 7, 1930. The order of the Central Executive Committee to end the various local merchant-civilian associations was not promulgated until February 10, 1930. Before the central government had unified merchant organization laws and regulations, this committee could not start work. Second, to unify the organization, it was necessary to change and reorganize the previously ununified merchant organizations first. The initial step in the reorganization was registration. The registration of merchant organizations in this city was originally a pioneering undertaking, so at the beginning, some organizations simply did not pay attention to it and did not take it seriously. Some organizations simply had misunderstandings, so it was necessary to extend the deadline for registration to the end of October. The second step was reorganization. The meaning of reorganization is to transform illegal organizations into legal organizations, and to merge organizations of the same nature that should be merged according to law. However, each industry organization has its own long history and separate relationships. In the past, they were used to being left alone. Once the laws and regulations promulgated by the central government were seriously implemented, there were bound to be many difficulties. Therefore, there were even cases where public documents requesting reconsideration of the change of name of a trade association were received three or four times in a row. The difficulties encountered in reorganizing and merging organizations according to law were naturally even greater. Fortunately, the central government and the municipal party and government organs presided over and guided from above, and the various industry organizations gradually understood the true meaning of the reorganization by this committee, so they were still able to complete the procedures for preparing the municipal chamber of commerce within a year. On the one hand, this allowed this committee to live up to the mission of the central government, and on the other hand, it organized merchant organizations according to law. When the whole country is calculated, Shanghai is still the first success, and it is considered not to have failed Shanghai's consistently advanced status in all matters. On behalf of all the members of this committee, I should express my sincere gratitude. This is the meaning of today's meeting.

Report of the General Meeting The Chairman reported, "The meaning of today's meeting has just been explained by Chairman Yu. Now, I will report on the results of the registration and reorganization handled by this committee. The tasks of this committee, in accordance with Article 3 of the organizational outline of this committee, which was revised and approved by the 14th Standing Committee meeting of the Central Committee on May 23, 1929, are stipulated as (1) registering the members of the former Shanghai Merchant-Civilian Association, Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, Zhabei Chamber of Commerce, and Nanshi Chamber of Commerce; (2) drafting the charter of the unified organization according to laws and regulations; (3) preparing all organizational procedures for the unified organization. Article 5 of the same outline stipulates that other local merchant organization matters may be guided by this committee in accordance with laws and regulations. Now, on behalf of this committee, I will report the progress of various matters to all representatives. First, is the registration issue. The organizational outline of this committee stipulates that the registration method shall be determined separately, so after the establishment of this committee, it drafted registration regulations and submitted them to the central government for approval and implemented the registration. For the final deadline, this committee also issued a notice in conjunction with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters Public Education Committee, stating that registration is an indispensable procedure for all commercial organizations in the city. If it is not done by the deadline, not only will requests submitted thereafter not be accepted, but there will also be grounds for banning and dissolving them. In total, 261 organizations were registered throughout the city. By analysis, 71 previously belonged to the Merchant-Civilian Association, 77 belonged to the General Chamber of Commerce, 3 belonged to the Zhabei Chamber of Commerce, 32 belonged to the Nanshi Chamber of Commerce, 56 had not previously joined the four merchant organizations, and 18 were special organizations (i.e., hometown organizations and national goods united organizations, etc.). This is the first item of this committee's task regarding the handling of registration matters that can be reported. Second, is drafting the charter of the unified organization according to laws and regulations. Since the promulgation of the Chamber of Commerce Law, this committee, at its 7th plenary meeting on August 28, 1929, appointed Wang Xiaolai, Lu Fengzhu, Xu Jilu, Fang Jiaobo, Yan Esheng, Lu Qisheng, Qin Runqing, and others as members of the Chamber of Commerce charter drafting committee. After the Ministry of Industry and Commerce promulgated the implementing regulations for the Chamber of Commerce Law, they immediately started drafting. At the same time, the committee repeatedly telegraphed the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to promptly promulgate the implementing regulations for the Chamber of Commerce Law. It was not until January of this year that the implementing regulations for the Chamber of Commerce Law were issued by the Ministry. The drafting committee then drafted the full text of the draft, totaling 11 chapters and 60 articles. It was passed by the 10th plenary meeting on February 22 of this year and sent to the Social Affairs Bureau for submission to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. On May 16, the Social Affairs Bureau replied, stating that the draft charter had been revised and submitted to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. Except for the proportional method of collecting membership fees, which was drafted in accordance with the Chamber of Commerce Law, all other cases were handled in accordance with the revised draft. It was further resolved at the 51st Standing Committee meeting on May 19 that the proportional method of collecting membership fees would be discussed and decided at the general meeting of members' representatives, and all other items would be revised and sent to the Social Affairs Bureau for record. This charter, which has been submitted for approval and record, will be read out article by article, except for the article on membership fees, which will be discussed as a separate proposal. This is the second item of this committee's task regarding drafting the charter of the unified organization that can be reported. Third, is preparing all organizational procedures for the unified organization. To complete the organization of the unified organization, it is necessary to thoroughly reorganize the registered organizations. As the name suggests, this is also the most important part of the responsibility borne by this committee. However, the premise of reorganization is "according to law." This committee can use the following to guide various organizations in reorganization: (1) the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law promulgated by the National Government; (2) the implementing regulations for the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law promulgated by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce; (3) the reorganization rules submitted by this committee for approval; (4) the reorganization and organizational procedures submitted by this committee for approval; and the approval orders of the Central Executive Committee, the Central Training Department, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and the Municipal Government for various organizational and reorganization issues. The most important aspects of the reorganization method are two points: A. All organizations in the city that do not have the same organization, regardless of whether they previously used the names guild hall, association, public association, branch, or joint association, shall change their names to a certain industry trade association of the Shanghai Special Municipality or a certain industry trade association of the Shanghai Special Municipality in accordance with Article 1 of the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law. B. If there are more than one organization in the city in the same industry, the number of reorganization committee members that each organization should recommend shall be determined by this committee according to the proportion of the number of members of each organization. These organizations should organize an industry organization reorganization committee to carry out the reorganization and establish the industry trade association within a time limit. If the organization cannot recommend reorganization committee members, this committee will investigate the central figures of the organization and appoint them. In addition to the above-mentioned reorganized and merged organizations, there are also organizations that request new organization. This committee has also followed the organizational plan of people's organizations promulgated by the National Government and the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law to guide their legal organization. In total, the number of reorganized, merged, and newly organized industry trade associations is 170. By analysis, 140 were reorganized, 58 were merged into 23, and 7 were newly organized. In addition to the above-mentioned various organizations, there are also (1) 17 organizations with fluidity; (2) 8 stallholder organizations; (3) 3 joint organizations of more than one industry; (4) 12 joint organizations above the regional level; (5) 10 organizations with a regional scope; (6) 5 national goods united organizations; (7) 7 hometown organizations; (8) 5 organizations with stallholder organizations and regional characteristics; (9) 1 organization that requested cancellation; (10) 1 organization that the Social Affairs Bureau instructed not to reorganize; and (11) 1 organization that was virtually suspended. The above total of 66 organizations are not in the reorganization list. Except for the three organizations that requested cancellation, were virtually suspended, and were instructed by the Social Affairs Bureau not to reorganize, the reasons for not reorganizing all other organizations are: A. Although this committee has stated the reasons for the organizations of fluid stallholders to organize, the Central Training Department and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce have replied that they believe that they cannot organize industry trade associations according to law and should be dissolved immediately. B. Joint organizations of more than one industry and national goods united organizations should be sent to the Legislative Yuan to formulate separate regulations in accordance with the resolution of the 55th meeting of the Executive Yuan this year and are not within the scope of the Chamber of Commerce Law. C. Joint organizations above the regional level, organizations with a regional scope, and hometown organizations all have the characteristics of being based on local units and do not meet the qualifications of members of the Chamber of Commerce in Article 9 of the Chamber of Commerce Law. According to the instructions of the Central Training Department No. 2255, they should join various industry trade associations according to their nature and do not need to be stipulated separately. Of course, they cannot join the Chamber of Commerce. In addition, there is another issue that should be reported incidentally, that is, since the National Government promulgated the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law, should the industry trade associations in this city that were organized according to the separate charters promulgated by the competent ministries in the past be reorganized according to law? The Standing Committee of this committee also resolved to submit it to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for verification. Subsequently, it received the approval of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce No. 8929, stating that all industrial and commercial enterprises in the Republic of China should abide by the Industrial and Commercial Trade Association Law promulgated by the National Government. Separate charters should be judged by whether they conflict with this law, etc. This committee has followed this approval order and has notified various associations organized according to separate charters to reorganize according to law. The above points are the third item of this committee's task, preparing all organizational procedures for the unified organization, that can be reported. The third task of this committee has now been reported. There are still two things that should be reported. The first is the number of member representatives who reported to the general meeting. It has been reported above that there are 170 industry trade associations with a common law. At this session of the general meeting of members' representatives, the number of industry trade associations that have recommended representatives is currently 142, which is calculated to be more than two-thirds. The total number of representatives recommended by the organizations is 346. In addition, shop members, according to the Chamber of Commerce Law, are limited to those in the city who do not have the same industry or who have the same industry but do not have an industry trade association. However, the so-called those who have the same industry but do not have an industry trade association, does the interpretation refer to those who have can legally organize an industry trade association (i.e., must have seven or more firms in the same industry) but do not want to organize or have not yet organized, or is it limited to those who have less than seven firms in the same industry and cannot legally organize an industry trade association? There are no clear provisions in the laws and regulations, so the first representative qualification review committee of this committee, when it met on the 17th of this month, used the first type, those who have can legally organize an industry trade association but do not want to organize or have not yet organized, as the review standard. On the morning of the 18th, it received the approval order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce No. 10894, which stated that the so-called those who have the same industry but do not have an industry trade association mentioned in Article 6 of the Chamber of Commerce Law refers to those who have less than seven firms in the same industry in the same area. If there are seven or more firms, they should immediately organize an industry trade association according to law, and the association should send representatives to join the Chamber of Commerce. The provisions of shop members in that article cannot be applied to conform to the legal system and avoid disputes, etc. In accordance with this approval order, there are clear restrictions on shop members. This committee then convened the second meeting of the member qualification review committee on the 19th to review again. As a result of the review, there were 19 shop members who were deemed qualified by the first review committee meeting but conflicted with the approval order of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. They were immediately informed to withdraw from membership and the prepaid attendance fee was returned. Now, there are 10 shop members who have been re-examined and qualified, totaling 23 representatives. Together with the organization member representatives, the total is 369 member representatives. This should be reported as one. The second item, Article 49 of the Chamber of Commerce charter stipulates that the fund for the public bonds issued by this committee should be increased by 30% according to the amount of membership fees until the public bonds are repaid. This fund should be kept by a separate custody committee. The collection of attendance fees at this session of the general meeting of representatives is also based on this charter, with an increase of 30%, which is 15 yuan for organization member representatives and 9 yuan for shop member representatives. Except for the public bond fund custody committee, which should be organized separately after the executive and supervisory committee members of the Chamber of Commerce are elected, all public bonds that should be repaid should be reported separately below: (A) The former General Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds. According to the 23rd meeting of the board of directors of the General Chamber of Commerce on November 28, 1916, the construction of the meeting hall and office buildings of this association has been completed successively. The construction cost is still huge in addition to donations and fundraising, and it has all been borrowed. It is urgent to raise funds to repay the debt. In addition, the case of preparing for the product exhibition hall was unanimously advocated for construction, but there was no way to prepare for the construction. It was resolved that the insufficient funds for the construction of the meeting hall and the construction funds for the exhibition hall should be raised by issuing public bonds to offset the debt. For the repayment of principal and interest, 30% should be added to the membership fees as a fund. Subsequently, at the 24th meeting of the board of directors on December 2 of the same year, it was resolved to raise 80,000 taels of debt, print 1,600 bonds, each worth 50 taels, and repay the principal and interest in twelve years. In addition to those that have been repaid, there is currently an outstanding debt of 17,576 taels, 1 mace, and 6 candareens. (B) The former General Chamber of Commerce reorganization public bonds. According to the first meeting of the board of directors on January 4, 1926, during the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War in 1925, troops gathered, supplying grain and fodder, supporting scattered soldiers, and taking over the Shanghai Arsenal, which cost a lot. In addition, after the May 30th Massacre occurred, the stalemate lasted for a long time, donations from all parties gradually dried up, and the expenses for the Yarn Factory workers to start work subsidies and seafarer relief were all temporarily borrowed and gathered by the association. Except for those borrowed from the government with evidence, the remaining short-term borrowings have no collateral. The lunar New Year is approaching in an instant, and all must be repaid to maintain credit. The precedent of the former construction public bonds was followed to issue reorganization public bonds of 100,000 taels, each worth 100 taels. The construction public bonds will be deducted until the end of the 17th year, and the 30% fund after the construction public bonds are repaid will still be used to pay the principal and interest of this public bond, which will be repaid in twelve years. The current outstanding debt on this bond is 138,209 taels. (C) The former Shanghai South Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds. In 1924, the old meeting hall in Maojia Lane was not sufficient for office work, so the board of directors resolved to build a new meeting hall. The former chairman Yao Ziruo and vice chairman Yao Mulian were responsible for preparing. First, more than 40,000 taels were accumulated to purchase more than four acres of open space on Zhonghua Road, Xiaonanmen. Drawings were made and construction was estimated, and it was estimated that at least 150,000 yuan would be needed. The board of directors also discussed in detail and decided to follow the example of the General Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds to issue former Shanghai County Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds worth 60,000 taels of standard silver, with each ticket worth 100 taels, totaling 600 tickets, with an annual interest rate of 9%, to be repaid in ten years. The interest was paid only in the first period, and the principal and interest were paid from the second period. The end of June in the Gregorian calendar each year was the date for repaying the principal and interest. It was supposed to be repaid in full by 1935. Since being ordered to merge in May of the 18th year, the repayment of principal and interest has been delayed by two periods. The current outstanding debt on this bond is 60,576 taels, 6 mace, and 3 candareens. The total outstanding debt on the above three public bonds is 216,361 taels, 7 mace, and 9 candareens. Except for the former Shanghai South Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds, which still have rental income to offset the bonds, the remaining former General Chamber of Commerce construction public bonds and reorganization public bonds should all be repaid in installments from the 30% fee attached. This should be reported as two. The above reports total five items, but they only cover the most important ones. As for the detailed report of this committee's work, it will be compiled into a special book after the committee's work is completed and distributed to all members and representatives for review.

Admonitory Speech by the Central Representative Everyone, Shanghai is a commercial center, and the organization of commercial organizations has always been complex and uneconomical. This time, the Consolidation Committee was ordered to reorganize the commercial organizations in this city. It took a year to complete the reorganization. Although it has not been completed for all industries and organizations in the city, the spirit has already been unified. Shanghai is the most important commercial port in the country. To develop the national industrial and commercial undertakings, it is natural to start from Shanghai. Therefore, the establishment of a unified organization today is a very good thing. I am very honored to participate in this general meeting of representatives. The Chamber of Commerce is the leading organization of commercial organizations in the city and bears a great mission. I hope that everyone will work together to promote the development of industry and commerce and realize it. The Premier also had a plan to develop industrial and commercial undertakings. The Third National Congress has a resolution to implement it. Measures to improve products, promote domestic goods, and inspect products are all aimed at breaking down obstacles to industry and commerce and seeking their development. Today, the Chamber of Commerce is established. I still hope that everyone will work together to assist in the completion of a good commercial organization to serve as an example and provide great assistance to the government.

Admonitory Speech by the Representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters Everyone, today all the representatives are here to participate. I think everyone understands that they bear a heavy responsibility. Why does Shanghai have such an organization to reorganize merchant organizations? Because the central government hopes that Shanghai will have a sound merchant organization to help the government develop industry and commerce. In the past, merchants had a saying "in business, speak of business."

Page 14

In fact, these four words are a fallacy that merchants have no national concept. We hope that after the Chamber of Commerce is established in the future, it will rise up to seek more welfare for merchants and develop industrial and commercial undertakings. However, to seek industrial and commercial development, the first point should be to maintain the original industrial and commercial enterprises. Now, the leather, soap, match, shipping, silk, and satin industries are gradually declining. The original industrial and commercial enterprises cannot be maintained, so how can we seek development? Therefore, to develop industrial and commercial enterprises, we must first maintain the original enterprises. Therefore, we hope that the Chamber of Commerce should pay attention to this first. The second point is the unemployment problem. The pharmaceutical industry turmoil this year is that the unemployment problem has affected various drugstores and prevented them from opening for business. Therefore, to develop industrial and commercial enterprises, we must first solve the unemployment problem. The third point is that the majority of our country's people are poor. At least 100 million people have an income of less than 130 yuan per year. Due to the livelihood of the poor, goods cannot be sold as much as possible. Even if industrial and commercial enterprises want to develop, there is no way to solve the problem thoroughly. The fourth point is that industrial and commercial undertakings cannot develop if the situation cannot be peaceful and unified. The fifth point is the economic aggression of foreign merchants. Foreign merchants have developed commerce in China, such as banks, shipping, and yarn factories, occupying the largest force in Shanghai. Chinese commerce and finance are only 600 million yuan, and foreign merchants account for half of it. There are the above five reasons, so to break through the difficulties of industrial and commercial enterprises, there should be a sound organization to assist the government and find ways to remedy the situation. If these five problems cannot be solved, our country's industrial and commercial enterprises are a dead end. In the past, the Chamber of Commerce only focused on dealing with officialdom and neglected the development of commerce. Now, the most important responsibility of the Chamber of Commerce is to make the development of industrial and commercial enterprises the first priority.

Official Instructions from the National Government's Ministry of Industry, Commerce, and the Municipal Government Representative 116

Just now, the representative from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Mr. Zhao Jinqing, has left, entrusting me to represent him. Therefore, today I represent the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. Today, those participating in this conference include representatives from various party and government organs, who have already delivered excellent and detailed speeches. I could have remained silent, but regarding how to develop China's industry and commerce, Comrade Tao has already spoken, and I have some supplementary ideas to offer to you all. I ask for your attention. Comrade Tao said that China's only way out is to develop industry and commerce, and to develop industry and commerce, the five obstacles he mentioned must be completely overcome. To overcome these obstacles, one must understand that nothing in the world can be achieved without effort. The mentality of attributing success to luck and relying on fate must be completely eradicated. To achieve something, one must have the necessary strength. In the past, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce could not shoulder this mission. The most significant reason was the flawed organizational structure. Because the previous Chamber of Commerce was based on individuals. Someone joining the Chamber of Commerce meant they were a respectable merchant. Everyone was focused on themselves, not on industry and commerce. Therefore, they could not accomplish anything. Now, the focus is on the industry itself. The Chamber of Commerce is a united organization of various industrial and commercial guilds, based on industry and commerce. This point should be clear to everyone. Everyone here is a representative of the members, not just a member. Just now, the chairman reported that the merger of all 170 organizations in Shanghai into the Chamber of Commerce has been resolved. From now on, we will jointly develop China's industry and commerce. As long as everyone is willing to work hard, the country's industry and commerce can be saved. Because Shanghai is the most important place for industry and commerce, the place with the most power. If Shanghai's industrialists and merchants can shoulder this responsibility, the whole country will have a solution. The disunity and lack of peace that Comrade Tao mentioned are also obstacles to the development of industry and commerce. If these obstacles are not resolved, industry and commerce cannot develop. How can industry and commerce develop when there is fighting? Everyone knows, when did England's industry and commerce flourish? It was after Elizabeth unified England. Under a unified government, England's industrial and commercial enterprises could flourish. Similarly, Germany did so after Prussia established the German Confederation, and Japan did so after the Meiji Restoration. It can be seen that no country in the world has been able to develop industry and commerce under a disunified government. Now, in Tianjin, Yan Xishan has put a foreign rogue in charge of the customs as a customs commissioner. The National Government's response is to order the closure of Tianjin Customs. This approach causes suffering for our merchants. Goods that were shipped to Tianjin for export now have to be transported back. Merchants suffer from this, and those who do not understand the situation will surely blame the Nanjing government. In reality, they are suffering because of Yan Xishan. Similarly, if bandits cause trouble inland, there are still solutions within the National Government's territory. However, if it is within the territory controlled by the rebellious army, there is no solution. Therefore, to develop the country's industry and commerce, we must use our entire strength to seek national peace and unification, and not just treat the symptoms without addressing the root cause. For example, the rebels of Yan and Feng rely on money to cause chaos. We must at least cut off their economic supply so that unification can be hoped for. Only when unification is in sight can we plan for the development of industry and commerce. My supplementary idea to Comrade Tao is that we must first unify the political situation before we can develop industry and commerce. Therefore, I hope that everyone will work together to promote unification and develop industry and commerce. At the same time, I would like to report to everyone present that the Chamber of Commerce Preparatory Committee received a telegram from the National Government's Secretariat today, appointing Mayor Zhang to represent the National Government to address the meeting. Mayor Zhang is too busy with official duties, so he sent me to attend. This is a combined statement.

The representative of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce said briefly, "I am honored to attend and participate today on behalf of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce. In the past, the General Chamber of Commerce had a glorious history, and it was the beginning of the Chamber of Commerce in China, established in the seventeenth year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, which is now thirty years ago. However, these thirty years have been through many storms. Today, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is established. I hope that all of you present will be able to invigorate your spirits and seek benefits for commerce. The last sentence is that there is the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, then the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, and then the Chamber of Commerce Law. Please pay attention to this."

Chairman's Closing Remarks: Chairman Xu Jiqing said in his closing remarks, "Under the guidance of the Party, the merchants have a unified organization for a grand gathering. Not to mention that it is a groundbreaking event in this city, I am afraid it is also a groundbreaking event in the whole country. Therefore, although today's conference has ended, its value is indelible and will always be worth remembering. From another perspective, today's gathering of members is the beginning of a new life for merchants. Therefore, when I am about to conclude this meeting, on the one hand, I would like to thank the party and government organs and all the guests for their presence and guidance on behalf of all the members of the general assembly. On the other hand, I also hope that from today onwards, all members will make unremitting efforts. Time is short, and I cannot say more. I hope you will understand."

Resolutions of Various Proposals: (A) Proposals from the General Assembly: (1) Request both labor and management to jointly respect the Labor-Management Dispute Resolution Law and request the National Government to reaffirm the order to protect human rights in order to eliminate extra-legal actions in labor-management disputes. (2) The trade regulations submitted by various trade associations for approval and record by the competent authorities should be regarded as special regulations for the industry formulated by the authorities, and non-member industries should jointly abide by them. (3) How should appropriate protection be planned to safeguard navigation rights in response to foreign vessels arbitrarily colliding with Chinese ships? (4) Plan to establish Chamber of Commerce branch offices in Wusong River Bay, Pudong, and Qibao. Resolutions: All four proposals were passed in principle and handed over to the first executive committee for review. (5) The proposed trial budget for the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce for the nineteenth year is requested to be passed. Resolution: Passed. (6) The proposed proportion of annual membership fees for Chamber of Commerce members is included in Article 46 of Chapter 9 of the Chamber of Commerce Constitution and is requested to be passed. After discussion, six items were added and passed. (7) The staffing of the Chamber of Commerce office will temporarily set up one office and three sections, and after a year of trial operation, detailed rules for the division of sections will be formulated and submitted for public decision. Resolution: Passed in principle and handed over to the executive committee for handling. (8) (B) Temporary Motions: (1) Notify all merchant organizations in the city and advise merchants to practice using domestic products. Resolution: Passed. (2) Request party, government, and military agencies to follow the orders of the National Government and implement the use of domestic products. Resolution: Passed.

Mayor Zhang's

Important Remarks on the Current Situation 117

Yesterday morning, reporters from various newspapers went to the Municipal Government to meet Mayor Zhang and inquire about the current situation. Mayor Zhang graciously received them. The following is the conversation between the reporters and Mayor Zhang. Reporter asked (hereinafter referred to as ask): Japanese newspapers reported that Mayor Zhang visited Mr. Yu Youren to conduct peace talks. Is this true? Mr. Zhang replied (hereinafter referred to as reply): Mr. Yu has been ill recently, so I don't see him often. When we do meet, we just have casual conversations. The reports are completely unfounded. (Ask): Japanese newspapers have been spreading similar rumors recently. What is the reason for this? (Reply): This kind of provocative, divisive, and schadenfreude behavior does not seem like the national character of the Japanese people. However, the reason why they must do this must be related to other factors. They have to act as propaganda for the reactionaries. For example, Japanese newspapers have twice reported that Mr. Zhang Jingjiang is working for peace, and recently they said that Yang Hucheng and Xu Yuanquan have rebelled. In fact, all of these are unfounded. Everyone knows this. Such dishonest behavior is just deceiving themselves. There is no need for me to say anything more. I remember that Mr. Yamada, the Japanese Minister to China during the late Qing Dynasty, once said that what harms the friendly relations between China and Japan is the frivolousness of newspaper reporters' remarks. Duke Ito also said that newspaper reporters should be responsible for the order and chaos of the world. These unconscious newspaper reporters cannot comprehend the famous sayings of the sages. I really think this is the biggest flaw of mankind and should be despised by the discerning. We should jointly correct this and sanction it so that the few people with ulterior motives will disappear from now on, in order to enhance the friendly relations between China and Japan. (Ask): Japanese newspapers reported from Beiping that Yan Xishan has returned to Taiyuan with important officials, and that the headquarters will also be moved from Shijiazhuang. When the war is urgent, why doesn't he go to the front to supervise the army, but instead retreats? (Reply): Yan's rebellion this time was forced by the environment and may not have been his original intention. When the war began, Yan had a total of 64 regiments, about 90,000 men. Because Feng was responsible for military affairs and Yan himself was responsible for political affairs, Yan gave 50,000 men to Feng to command. Unfortunately, they lost more than half in the battle across the river. The remaining small number of more than ten regiments on the Jinpu Railway attempted to cross the river and occupy Jinan, but the plan also failed. The remaining troops in the northern section of the Pinghan Railway and in the rear could not be mobilized. Therefore, he is in a military dead end. And the political responsibility he bears is not only that the government cannot be organized and established, but also that the foreign affairs and financial plans have failed. Even the recent seizure of the Tianjin Customs shows his boredom. As for party affairs, there is no history to speak of. Now that military and political affairs are in a dead end, and the propaganda of the Fengtian troops being sent is in full swing, we can conclude that Yan's return to Taiyuan will be a consideration of his own position and a discussion of his aftermath plans. (Ask): What is Mayor Zhang's observation on the future of the war situation? (Reply): Yan's current situation is already like this, and Zhang Gui in Hunan is also surrounded and easily annihilated. The Central Army completely dominates the battlefields of Longhai and Pinghan. The future of the war does not need to be known by those with military knowledge. (Ask): Since the future is so optimistic, why was there news of the retreat of the Pinghan Central Army a few days ago? (Reply): This is not something that outsiders can know. The movement of the Pinghan Central Army is called repairing the front line in military terms. It is a tactic that must be adopted to change positional warfare into mobile warfare. The rebel army does not know this and regards it as a forced retreat, which is a big mistake. This is the main reason why they are dominated by the Central Army on the battlefield. Nothing in the world can be won if you do not know yourself and know your enemy. (Ask): How many days will it take to end the war? (Reply): According to my estimation, it will take at most one month to end. At this point, Mayor Zhang's pre-arranged foreign guests arrived, and the reporters excused themselves and left.

Gold Price Rose Again Yesterday 119

Highest at 615 Taels

The price of gold soared again yesterday. The price of gold had been rising continuously for several days, but it was always within 610 taels. Unexpectedly, it broke the unprecedented new record yesterday. The highest price on the exchange was 615 taels, and it closed at 612.5 taels. The price of gold jewelry at Dahang was 84 yuan. The market is chaotic and people are panicking. No one knows where this will end.

American Silver Still Arriving in Shanghai: The mail ships from San Francisco to Shanghai still arrive once a week, carrying silver bars each time of about one million taels to Shanghai. However, because the customs prohibits landing, when the last two mail ships arrived in Shanghai, only 198 bars out of 828 on the first ship were allowed to be unloaded in Shanghai. Of the 925 bars on the second ship, only 175 were allowed to land. The rest were diverted to Hong Kong for unloading.

Hong Kong Bans Silver Imports: With the Shanghai ban on silver imports, large bars that should have been unloaded in Shanghai are mostly going to Hong Kong, resulting in a large increase in Hong Kong's silver reserves. Shanghai also often has large shipments of Mexican dollars going there. Yesterday, we received a telegram from Hong Kong that the Hong Kong government has also issued a ban on the import of silver and Mexican dollars. Shanghai's silver coins can no longer be shipped in large quantities.

The Japanese Rumor of 121

The Pacific Illegal Immigration Group

Scamming Money

Killing Lives

According to Japanese sources, an extremely terrifying secret illegal immigration conspiracy has occurred in the Pacific shipping industry. The discovery of this matter was still in the autumn of last year. It seems that there is an illegal immigration group on the Eastern coast (including Shanghai, Hong Kong, Japan, and other places), and the person in charge seems to be a certain national. The method is to send members to major ports to contact travelers who are not qualified to go to the United States but are determined to go. The group will take responsibility for bringing passengers on board so that they can cross the ocean to reach the United States without being hindered. The price for guaranteeing illegal immigration is divided into about three categories: the largest is 1200 yuan, the second is 700 yuan, and the smallest is 500 yuan. It is said that many people have been fooled and have smuggled overseas. Most of them pay half the amount first, and the rest is paid after arriving. However, after this case occurred, those who set off disappeared. In August and September of last autumn, the Japanese authorities conducted strict inspections of this matter and prohibited newspapers from publishing it. At that time, a fooled Japanese person risked his life to escape halfway, and the secret of the illegal immigration group was gradually known to the world. The other day, a certain ship came to Shanghai from the United States, and another Japanese person who was fooled but not harmed was found out and sent back to Shanghai. It is said that after the group tricked half of the money from the smuggled passengers, they would agree to board the ship together. When the ship sailed into the Pacific Ocean, they would use poison, lure the passengers to the deck, and have their accomplices tie them up and throw them into the ocean. This would not only silence them, but also get a huge amount of money. It is said that the number of people who have been lured to their deaths and thrown into the ocean by these people is unknown. Now that this matter has been exposed, the ship inspectors are also extra strict.

Planning to Sell Daughter into Prostitution 122

Daughter Cries and Refuses

Mother Whips Her

Finally Swallows Opium and Commits Suicide

The Yangzhou girl Yan Yue'e, who lives at No. 5 Anren Lane, Fuyou Road in the city, is a beautiful young woman of fourteen years old. She once studied at a nearby elementary school and knows a little bit of literacy. Later, she assisted her mother in managing the household affairs, so she dropped out of school and worked as a needlewoman at home. Unexpectedly, her father, who had been out of work for a long time and had a difficult life, planned to sell his beloved daughter to a brothel to make a living by selling her smiles. However, the plan was not kept secret, and the girl heard about it. She tearfully pleaded with her mother, saying that she did not want to fall into the world of prostitution and begged her mother to help her. Unexpectedly, her mother was ashamed and angry and whipped her. Under the pain, Yue'e knew that her parents' will was firm and could not be reversed. It would be better to leave this world early and avoid a life of selling her flesh. So she decided to commit suicide. Yesterday afternoon, she secretly swallowed opium paste behind people's backs. After being discovered by her family, she was rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment. However, the medicine was ineffective, and she died at around 6 PM.

Committed Two Murder Cases

The bandit Jiang Jigui (also known as Zhang Jigui) shot and killed Cao Buhua, the owner of a teahouse on Jungong Road, in August of the 16th year of the Republic of China. On January 30th of the 18th year of the Republic of China, Wu Tingyao, a patrol officer of the fourth precinct of the fifth district, was searching pedestrians on the road, and Jiang opened fire and killed the patrol officer. After investigation by Yang Wenxun, the prosecutor of the local court, he filed a public prosecution on the grounds that the criminal had committed multiple major murder cases. Judge Wu Zhen opened the court for trial. After the debate was over, the judge and prosecutor opened the court yesterday to pronounce the verdict. Jiang Jigui persisted in evil and could not be forgiven by the law and was abandoned by society. Therefore, Jiang was sentenced to death and deprived of public rights for life. After the sentence was pronounced, he was ordered to be returned to prison to await reporting to the superior for review and execution.

Lawsuit Regarding Inheritance between Mother and Son 128

Mother Says Son Slanders

Son Says Mother Occupies

Yu Longzhang of Ningbo, residing at No. 17 Dong Street, Xiaodongmen, has recently stated that after the death of his father, Yu Jinlin, all the inherited property was seized and occupied by his father's concubine, Yu Cai, and his requests were ignored. Therefore, he entrusted lawyer Chen Wenzhao to publish a statement in the newspaper, roughly stating that any transfer or disposal of the property would not be valid unless Longzhang personally signed it. Yu Cai also hired a lawyer to publish a rebuttal in the newspaper, stating that Yu Cai was Yu Jinlin's successor wife, and should not be deliberately slandered and her reputation damaged. She then filed a self-accusation with the Criminal Court of the District Court, stating that Yu Longzhang had committed two counts of slander. Yu Longzhang, still represented by lawyer Chen, filed a lawsuit with the Civil Court of the District Court, stating that the defendant Yu Cai was occupying the inheritance and concealing the receipts, requesting a judgment to return the property for management. He also stated that during his late father Jinlin's lifetime, he formally married Jin, who bore three children. The plaintiff is the only son, the elder sister is married, and the younger sister is not yet married. His late mother, Jin, died in the fourth year of the Republic of China. His late father had an affair with the defendant while he was away. Although they lived together later, she never obtained a formal status. Unfortunately, his late father passed away on May 2nd of this year. All the inheritance should naturally be legally inherited by the plaintiff. Unexpectedly, the defendant seized all the partnership shares and all the property that his late father had with others during his lifetime. She also published an obituary, claiming to be the successor wife, and referred to the distant cousin Yu Longbin as a mourning nephew. She regards the plaintiff as an enemy, while maintaining close contact with her daughter from her previous marriage. These actions clearly indicate an intention to endanger the property. Considering that his late father's lifetime of hard work resulted in various properties worth tens of thousands of dollars, the plaintiff married the year before last and has a son. Household expenses require money everywhere. Now that the defendant has seized everything, his livelihood is cut off. Therefore, he filed a lawsuit requesting a judgment to order the defendant to hand over all the property for management. Yesterday, the Criminal Court first summoned the case at 11:00 AM, presided over by Judge Deng Peiyi, who specially opened the eighth courtroom for the trial. The plaintiff and his lawyer, Dai, arrived in court, but the defendant was absent, represented by lawyer Chen Wenzhao. According to the plaintiff Yu Cai's testimony, she is 46 years old, from Ningbo, residing at No. 5 Yuyou Lane, Changsheng Bridge, Xiaodongmen. (Question) What is your relationship with Yu Jinlin? (Answer) He is my husband, and I am his concubine who became the legal wife, married in the fourth year of the Republic of China. (Question) When did Jinlin pass away? (Answer) May 2nd of this year. (Question) What is your relationship with Longzhang? (Answer) He is the son of his first wife. (Question) Why did you sue him? (Answer) He drove me out and ordered me to hand over the property, not acknowledging me as his mother, and saying that I was his father's mistress, damaging my reputation, so I sued him. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer presented the marriage certificate, family tree, obituary, and other documents for the court to examine. After reviewing them, the defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant had returned to Ningbo for business and had submitted a letter. He then described the defendant's age and origin, stating that Yu Longzhang, the defendant, is 20 years old, from Ningbo, residing at No. 17 Dong Street, Xiaodongmen. The plaintiff is accusing him of slander, but according to Article 339 of the Criminal Procedure Law, it does not apply between direct relatives, spouses, or family members living under the same roof. Therefore, the self-accusation is not legally valid. Furthermore, there is no crime of slander in fact, and the defendant has already had a son and should legally inherit the property. He requested the court to reject the self-accusation. He also submitted four copies of the newspaper articles published by both parties. The judge told the lawyers of both parties that this case is very clear and is entirely a civil dispute. Since the defendant is absent today, the hearing will be adjourned for further investigation. The court then adjourned.

Whereabouts of Robbers in Pudong 130

Woman's Testimony Suspicious

Robbers Deny Everything

They were then taken to the Special District Court. Detectives from the County Public Security Bureau brought the woman who reported the case to the court, along with an official document requesting transfer of custody. Judge Sun Yuan opened the court for a preliminary hearing. According to Fu Li's testimony, Shi Yuting also lived at No. 140, Route Lafayette, so she knew him. Since he moved to Qipu Road, the two families still visited each other frequently. On the 8th of this month, I went to Shi's home to gamble at mahjong and saw many people gathered there, with gold and silver jewelry, clothing, and bags scattered in the room. I paid close attention and later learned that they had been robbed from Pudong. At that time, they gathered to divide the spoils, so I reported it to the Public Security Bureau. My family runs a barbershop. On the 23rd of last month, an apprentice in the shop went missing, and we immediately searched for him. We happened to encounter the police searching, and I was carrying a package. The police, suspecting my behavior, took me to the Third Branch of the Third District. After I provided conclusive proof that the clothes in the package belonged to me, I was released. At the same time, Shi Yuting was also detained by the branch for carrying a package containing five leather garments. However, I do not know how he was released. Judge Sun found that the woman's testimony was full of discrepancies and difficult to understand. He ordered her to provide detailed information on how she knew Shi was one of the robbers in the case. The woman's answers were evasive and self-contradictory. Realizing that there must be another reason behind this, the court dismissed the woman and turned to Shi Yuting for questioning. Shi denied being a robber, saying that he was indeed acquainted with Chuan Li when he lived on Route Lafayette, but they separated due to some reason. I moved to Qipu Road, and I did not expect that she would hold a grudge and falsely accuse me of being a robber. Jin Shen testified that she was originally from Suzhou and came to Shanghai in March to work as a maid. She met Shi Yuting, and they fell in love and lived together. She knew nothing about the robbery. Judge Sun reviewed the testimony and ordered Shi Yuting and Jin Shen to be detained separately. Fu Li was asked to provide a shop address and a guarantor to ensure that she could be summoned at any time. The police were ordered to send detectives to the Third Branch of the Third District to inquire about whether they had intercepted the five leather garments and await further investigation.

Detectives Intercept Robbers on the Way 131

Four Men and Women Arrested in Succession

At 5:30 PM the day before yesterday, Hongkou Police Detective Mao Yiwen received a report that robbers were planning to go to Zhaojiadu to rob. He and detective Zhang Bingcheng, officer Yang Zhaoqing, and others armed themselves and waited at Jiangjiaqiao, Route Connaught, because it was a necessary route. Soon, Jin Zhongyi and Wu Ziming from Pudong came along, and their behavior seemed suspicious. Upon questioning, Wu became nervous and fled. They first arrested Jin and then chased after Wu and brought him back to the police station. Upon searching Jin, they found two loaded pistols on him, which were confiscated. Then, based on the information provided by the two men, they went to No. 25, Route Edward VII, and arrested another accomplice, Li Chengui, from Songjiang, in Swallow Nest. They found four bullets on him. Along with Li Su, a woman from Pudong who sold cigarettes, they were taken back to the police station. Yesterday morning, they were jointly taken to the Special District Court and interrogated by Judge Ge. According to Jin Zhongyi's testimony, yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM, a friend, Secretary Wang, gave me two loaded pistols and ordered me to take them to Zhaojiadu. I refused to carry them because I knew they were prohibited items. Wang said it was not for robbery and that there was no harm in carrying them. I was fooled and carried them for him. Wu Ziming was not traveling with me, and I do not know who he is. Wu testified that he was going to Zhaojiadu to borrow money from a friend. He was passing through the area and was arrested along with them. Li Chengui testified that the bullets on me were given to me by a friend surnamed Pan. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Li Su testified that Li Chengui often came to buy cigarettes, so I know him. I have never met Jin and Wu. Judge Ge, believing that the police still needed to investigate, ordered the defendants to be detained separately for further hearing.

Wuhu New Steamer Arrives in Shanghai 135

Unprecedented Fast Ship on the Yangtze River

First Trip on the 27th

British Swire Group, in order to expand its shipping business on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, has built a new type of diesel engine river steamer, named Wuhu, with a deadweight of 1,800 tons and a very high speed, capable of traveling 14 nautical miles per hour, which is one-third faster than existing ships. The ship arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong today and docked at the company's wharf in the French Concession. It is scheduled to operate exclusively on the Shanghai to Yichang route, stopping at Zhenjiang, Ningbo, Wuhu, Anqing, Jiujiang, Hankou, Yuezhou, Shashi, and other ports along the way. The ship is made entirely of steel, and the passenger cabins are divided into first, second, and third class. The design of the third-class cabin is particularly beautiful, with great emphasis on cleanliness and hygiene. A round trip is two or three days faster than other ships. A first-class cabin from Shanghai to Hankou costs only 40 yuan, and a second-class cabin costs 25 yuan. Le Jiaxiang has been appointed as the comprador. The passenger ticket business of this ship has been entrusted to China Travel Service, and the cargo business has been entrusted to Zhenda Company. After the ship arrives today, various parties will be invited to visit, and the maiden voyage to Yichang will be on the 27th.

Summer Office Hours of the Procuratorate 137

Attention to Litigants

The office hours of the local procuratorate in this port are from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM. Director Liu of the Procuratorate believes that the days are earlier in the summer and the afternoons are hot, which is inconvenient for both litigants and office workers. He now intends to follow the foreign system and change the daily office hours from July 1st to the end of August to 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM, with no office hours in the afternoon. In necessary circumstances, office hours may be extended at any time. As for the transfer of criminals by various agencies, except for important injuries that require urgent disposal, it is advisable to transfer them to the court as early as possible. A circular has been sent to various agencies for reference, and litigants are also informed to comply.

American Court Orders Chauffeur to Pay Compensation

She recovered after a month of treatment. Afterwards, she filed a complaint with the American Court against the motor company, demanding 2,000 US dollars in damages and 300 taels in medical expenses. Yesterday (20th), the American judge opened the court for trial. First, the doctor testified about the injuries, and then the plaintiff recounted the cause of the accident, saying that the chauffeur, Zhu A Long, seemed to be dozing off while driving. He drove from North Sichuan Road to Nanjing Road very well, but when turning onto Nanjing Road westbound, there were no pedestrians in the street, so there seemed to be no reason for the accident. The chauffeur, Zhu A Long, claimed that he was not dozing off while driving, but saw a child two feet in front of the car and turned the car to the right, causing it to collide with the lamppost. The judge said that no one else saw the alleged child, so it was difficult to believe, and ordered the defendant to pay 750 US dollars in compensation.

Japanese Expression on Tianjin Customs 144

Shigemitsu Has Telephoned the Japanese Government for Instructions

Japanese Collecting Taxes at Tianjin Customs on Behalf

After the northern forces forcibly seized the Tianjin Customs, the National Government has made a serious statement and ordered the blockade of the Tianjin Customs. All countries are paying close attention due to the relationship between customs duties and foreign debt guarantee funds. The Japanese Embassy received a telegram from Secretary Yano in Beiping yesterday, reporting the detailed situation. Acting Minister Shigemitsu telegraphed the Japanese government for instructions, but there is currently no concrete expression. However, according to a telegram from the Japanese Consul in Tianjin, Japanese merchant ships continue to import goods every day. Currently, because the customs officers of Tianjin Customs have been ordered to stop working, the Japanese Consulate has sent staff to the Customs to act as customs officers, performing duties, unloading goods from Japanese ships ashore, and collecting taxes as usual. However, the collected taxes are kept in the care of the Japanese Consul and will be returned to the legitimate Customs in the future. This special action of the Japanese has attracted the attention of various countries. The offices of the embassies of various countries in Shanghai have all considered it a major incident and have telegraphed their respective governments to report and request instructions.

Crisis of China's Tung Oil Industry in the United States 157

Report from the Consulate General in New York

Tung oil is a unique product of China, and the amount exported annually is enormous, especially to the United States. However, the United States has recently been promoting the cultivation and advocating for it in an effort to regain its own rights and interests. The impact of this is sufficient to harm the future of China's tung oil industry. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has received a report from the Consulate General in New York regarding the current situation and future prospects of Chinese tung oil in the United States, which is worthy of reference. The Ministry has instructed the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to inform them and to pass it on to Chinese tung oil merchants. An excerpt of the original report is as follows. It is hoped that tung oil operators in our country will pay close attention to it.

The Situation of Tung Oil Sales to the United States: Tung oil is a unique product of China. In recent years, the amount exported abroad has been enormous. The main destination for these sales is the United States, accounting for two-thirds of the total exports each year. According to a report by the US Department of Commerce, the amount of Chinese tung oil exported to the United States has been increasing by more than 10 million pounds per year, with a value increase of more than 1.5 million gold yuan per year, which is a noteworthy matter.

The Uses of Tung Oil in the United States: Tung oil is mainly used for making paints in the United States. The American-made oilcloth, linoleum, and other items rely entirely on tung oil as their sole raw material. American daily furniture, radios, automobiles, and steamships all require tung oil. Even fertilizers sometimes use it. Factories in the US rely on Tung Oil heavily.

The Success of American Trials: In view of the extensive uses of tung oil and its important position in industry, the United States has achieved remarkable results in recent years in trying to grow tung trees in Florida. The quality of the tung oil produced is superior, which is sufficient to compete with Chinese tung oil. However, the land suitable for planting tung oil in the United States is only in one area of Florida. The production can only supply a portion of the needs of the eastern United States. The needs of the central and western United States are still supplied by China. Therefore, the number of Chinese tung oil exports to the United States has continued to increase in recent years, which has attracted the attention of planters in the US. They plan to vigorously promote the planting of tung trees in the hope of increasing production to resist the import of Chinese tung oil.

Enthusiasm of Merchants for Promotion: An American named Berlin has organized a company in Miami, Florida, specializing in selling tung seeds to residents of the state. The company also has film lectures to guide the planting of tung trees and the ways to make profits. Advertisements are published in the local newspapers to make strange publicity to arouse the attention of Americans. Berlin Company recently published a full-page advertisement in the local newspaper, the Sun, titled "Do you want to make China's dream come true?" The content describes how China has monopolized the production and supply of tung oil to the world for fifty years, manipulating American industry. The people of the United States should break China's monopoly and work hard to plant tung trees. There is a free movie every night at 7:30 PM. Please listen to a special lecture on tung oil. The intention is very profound.

The Future of Chinese Tung Oil in the United States: In recent years, the United States has planted tung oil in Florida, achieving remarkable results, and the oil quality is far better than that of China. With the enthusiasm of merchants for patriotic publicity, the production of American tung oil in the future will be even more alarming. At present, the United States is still unable to supply enough, and it has no choice but to seek it from China. Once tung trees are planted everywhere and a large amount of tung oil is supplied, it will be difficult for Chinese tung oil to compete with it. As a precaution, China should quickly improve tung oil, improve quality, and persuade oil merchants to engage in large-scale manufacturing to reduce costs so as to compete with American products.

Central Bank Inspection Report 158

No. 57

The 57th issuance of Central Bank's reserve inspection report states, "According to the regulations in Article 15 of the Central Bank's articles, this committee is responsible for inspecting the reserves for the convertible notes issued by this bank. We have conducted the 57th inspection on the 20th of June, 1920 at the bank's issuance bureau. The results are announced as follows. The total amount of convertible notes issued is 15,971,501 silver yuan. 14,825,810 of that is in silver yuan notes and 1,145,691 is in supplementary coin notes. The total amount of the reserve for the convertible notes is 15,971,501 silver yuan. It is composed of 11,200,496.2 silver yuan in cash reserves. The cash reserves are 8,131,800.0032 yuan in the bank's issuance vault, 1,272,135.14 yuan in the branches of various cities, and 1,800,0560.07 yuan in other banks. The guaranteed reserve is 4,767,004.8 silver yuan. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, 60% should be in cash reserve and 40% in guaranteed reserves. The cash exceeds the 60% and the guarantee falls below the 40%, therefore it is in agreement with the regulations." This report is made on the 20th of June, 1920 by the chairman of the supervisory committee of the Central Bank, Li Fuxun, supervisors Wang Jingli, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, and Xu Jiqing.

Wife (in conflict with her husband): You are simply the most unconscious person in the world. I regret marrying you.
