Record of a Severed Arm: Traces of Tears at Baisha 170

If you were to visit a larger factory, you would often see workers without all ten fingers, with hands like mallets, some with only one arm, others blind in one eye, and some with a limp. The working ability of these disabled people is far inferior to that of healthy individuals. Yet, they are all employed there. If you do not know the underlying reason, you might think that the factory owner has a heart of Buddha, full of compassion, and is taking in these people. Little do you know that the reason they became disabled is similar to brave soldiers on the front lines, risking their lives on the battlefield, returning with flowers. Having suffered the tragedy of severed limbs and broken necks, those in charge have no choice but to find ways to accommodate them so they can eke out a living. The soldier's relation to the warlord and the worker's to the factory owner may differ in purpose, but their sacrifice for their superiors is the same. Having worked in factories for many years, I have witnessed dozens of cases of severed fingers and broken arms. However, I have never seen anything as tragic as what I saw the other day. I am writing down a brief account of it to tell the readers.

There was a man named Chen Jinlong, from Hunan Province, who was already in his forties. He came from a military background and was dismissed due to old age. He brought his wife and daughter to Shanghai to make a living. Through the introduction of his fellow villagers, he got a job at a cotton mill. His daughter, who was twelve years old, also worked with him. The father and daughter worked hard and earned just over ten yuan a month. His wife was in charge of cooking and washing. The three of them lived frugally, and they did not have to worry about starvation. This went on for about two months. However, one night, during the night shift, Jinlong and his daughter had just finished their midnight meal. The leather belt on the cotton-carding machine he was operating fell off. He rashly grabbed a ladder and leaned it against the ground shaft of the power source. He reached for the belt, trying to put it back on the pulley. Unfortunately, he used too much force, and no one was holding the ladder. As a result, the ladder slipped, and his hand was crushed by the pulley up to his arm. He fell to the ground unconscious, his hand still caught on the pulley, spinning with the shaft. Blood splattered everywhere, a gruesome sight. Co-workers heard the noise and rushed to see what happened, all crying out in alarm. When the manager arrived, he quickly ordered people to send him to the Shanghai East Hospital. On the way, he suddenly regained consciousness and said to those who were taking him, "Please, quickly shoot me in the head and kill me. This pain that pierces to the bone is unbearable." Upon arriving at the hospital, the doctor examined him and said his condition was critical. He finally died in the hospital around 5 AM. His wife was still asleep at the time. I entered the factory at 6 AM. Colleagues told me everything that had happened, as I described above. I also saw his severed arm wrapped in newspaper, a bloody mess. I couldn't bear to look at it. I was disturbed for days. The police were informed and took the body to Fellen Road for examination. The judge ruled that the factory should pay 300 yuan in compensation to settle the case. The next day, I saw his wife and daughter, with their heads uncovered and wearing mourning clothes, coming to the factory to receive the compensation. Their eyes were swollen like walnuts. I heard that the deceased had an elderly mother in her seventies back in his hometown.

Musings on the Opportunity: Fei Wenbao 171

A few days ago, a guest asked me what the highest gold price would be recently. I was reading the newspaper at the time and saw a section about free 606 injections. I casually answered, "606 taels." Unexpectedly, the next morning after the market opened, the highest price reached 606 taels. The price then quickly declined. The guest sold 14 gold bars around that time and treated me to a lavish meal at noon. After the feast, he called me a genius. When I told him how I arrived at the number, he smiled in embarrassment. This is a true example of seizing the moment! Ji Yun, also known as Ji Xiaolan, said, "When the opportunity arises, even ghosts and gods will seize it." Observing this event, I believe this more than ever. (Thank you)

Alas! Disaster can strike unexpectedly. It is truly a tragic occurrence. It shows that those who are not well-versed in mechanics and familiar with the structure of machines should not rashly handle them. Otherwise, accidents leading to disability or death are unavoidable. I have often advised workers of this principle, but ignorant people still create such tragedies from time to time. There is truly nothing that can be done.

The Emergence of Ms. Guan Zilan's Exhibition: Shiguang 172

Recently in Shanghai's art world, it seems there have been few Western painting exhibitions. Individual exhibitions are even rarer. The artistic atmosphere has been almost completely lifeless. Suddenly, on the eighth floor of the Hua'an Building, a noteworthy solo exhibition opened. It was Ms. Guan Zilan's contribution to society. Ms. Guan has a special sense for her subject matter. Where others find something ordinary and unnoticeable, she boldly paints it, surprising people by transforming these mundane scenes into beautiful places. Each of Ms. Guan's paintings is filled with emotion. Some are melancholic, like "Scenery of Xiling Bridge," "Lake Shadow," and "By the Pond." Others reveal a rich emotional outpouring, like a child quietly reminiscing about a loving sister. "Back Garden" and "Bamboo Fence Outside the Pavilion" feel even more profound. She transmits her emotions from her heart, through her wrist, and onto the canvas, allowing viewers to immediately perceive a sense of lightness and vibrant vitality.

Hanging in the second room is a large painting titled "Listening to Music." I find it to be her most emotionally expressive and fulfilling work. A young girl, with wide, clear eyes, seems completely absorbed in appreciating the sound of the music. Even a dog raises its neck, expressing its master's subtle feelings. A child in red clothing is also soothed by the lullaby-like music, bringing comfort to their innocent young life. Everything in the painting is entranced. The viewer seems to hear the beautiful music emanating from the strings and fingers, and is thus also entranced.

However, there is one point with which I am slightly dissatisfied: Ms. Guan does not distinctly differentiate light. Clothes, vases, and tree trunks all appear flat. However, this does not detract from the expression of her great descriptive power, nor does it mean that her paintings are flawed because of the lack of chiaroscuro. Perhaps this is her own special artistic choice.

In short, from these sixty or seventy works, we can clearly understand the greatness of Ms. Guan's artistic talent and be amazed at how she reveals her hidden emotions, breaking through the recent artistic silence in Shanghai.

Shen Tongqian in "The Merchant of Venice" 173

The play "The Merchant of Venice" is now being performed at the Danggui First Stage. One of the actors, Shen Tong, plays the greedy and hateful Shylock.

Mr. Shen is an old classmate of mine from Nanyang University. I recall that three or four years ago, when I was studying at Nanyang University, the student union had a drama group. They would put on a performance once or twice a semester. The talented individuals at that time included Tao Tianxing, Jia Cunjian, Xu Chuyun, and Yang Jiuquan.

A Letter Concerning Criticism of Mei Lanfang (Part 2) 174

As for the notion of a doctorate sweeping the floor, I believe Mr. Mei should not be blamed. My own footsteps have never left the country, and I am unaware of the depths of Western academia. However, I do know that those who diligently graduate, write theses, and obtain degrees are not necessarily beneficial to the nation. As for honorary degrees, the giver is merely expressing their admiration, and the recipient does not necessarily deserve the honor. If we were to measure their true learning, then those conferred upon by Xu Jurong and the various figures at Shanghai St. John's University, how would their scholarship compare? They would likely smile wryly to themselves. Why blame Mr. Mei alone? Moreover, Mr. Mei did not gain his reputation because of this. The public's aversion is something I, confined to the marketplace, have not yet heard of. Any dissenting opinions are mere speculation, lacking any verifiable evidence. The conclusion regarding the feelings of the adulators and the adulated is fascinating. However, those who offer praise, as I have presented, are engaged in open debate, and whether they are blindly praising is up to your esteemed judgment. I dare not presume. As for the person being praised, they are not originally seeking such accolades. They did not beg for it, so why should they feel ashamed? To promote virtue through art, without boasting or arrogance, I still believe Mr. Mei possesses such cultivation. This is what I dare to convey to you. Regarding your work, I have expressed my humble thoughts to the fullest extent. There are more things I wish to say: First, the Chinese tend to look down on successful people to make themselves feel superior. Second, they overvalue university degrees, especially those from the West. Third, the ingrained habit of belittling actors should be eradicated. Mr. Mei went to the United States to study and improve his craft, and fortunately, he succeeded. This is the result of his 20 years of dedicated study. The admiration of the Americans is also a result of their sincere appreciation and his utmost effort. It is not a mere formality. Therefore, why treat him as someone who is simply lucky? Moreover, music and drama share the same origins. When Chinese people go to America to study music, they often return with degrees, and I have not heard any controversy at that time. Therefore, the 20 years of stage experience of a dramatist can be compared to the five or six years of coursework of a scholar. The title of doctor may not be something to boast about, but to grant it to one and deny it to the other is excessive partiality. The ingrained habit that actors are not a respectable profession is a relic of the autocratic era, which you would not endorse. Today, so-called dramatic literature and popular education cannot do without this art form. If you insist on criticizing an actor for receiving a doctorate, it is akin to backward thinking. If we consider Shakespeare in England as an example, his writings and scholarship were concentrated upon by the English people. He was honored and praised because of his works and scholarship. Mr. Mei's stage experience and scripts are not necessarily inferior to Shakespeare's. Why are you critical of one and lenient towards the other? Furthermore, in the past, the famous Italian actor Caruso was performing in America when he fell seriously ill. The Italian king sent him a telegram of comfort, urging him to take care of himself for the sake of Italy. At that time, Italian immigrants and Americans were often at odds. However, the Americans were moved by Caruso's plays and gradually lessened their prejudice. Italy intended to expand its influence through subtle cultural influence and thus valued him highly. Today, when Mr. Mei goes abroad, he often states in his speeches that Americans can gain a better understanding of China and increase their goodwill. I am not suggesting that international formalities should add weight to Mr. Mei's significance. However, given the current state of China, as reported by Reuters, how would you, if you were an American, view such a nation? To have a Mei Lanfang who allows people to know that the ancient country of the East still has the path of music and art to offer is a remarkable achievement. I would like to offer you a toast for this. (The rest is omitted)

Xu Deyu, Shen Xueqian, and Yang Xiaozeng, among others. Mr. Shen is the most outstanding. Every time there was a play, Mr. Shen was always asked to play the villainous role. This is because his performance was profound, his pronunciation was clear, and he had a naturally villainous face. Once he put on makeup, he looked remarkably lifelike. In reality, Mr. Shen is of a gentle nature and has no villainous thoughts at all. However, he has such a villainous face. To judge a person by their appearance, Mr. Shen would be an exception.

The Shakespeare Drama Society performed the famous play "The Merchant of Venice." Some actors were perfectly suited to their roles, while others seemed a bit clumsy. I will not discuss them all. However, Mr. Shen's portrayal of the Jewish character Shylock, in his greed and wretchedness, was flawless. The grandeur of four or five years ago is still present today. If this play were performed in an old-style theater, Mr. Shen would undoubtedly be pelted with banana peels and sugarcane dregs.

After the play, because Mr. Shen's performance was even better than before, Yunxiu and I went backstage to visit him to express our admiration. Mr. Shen was modest and not complacent, saying that he would continue to work hard. I believe that Mr. Shen is a rare talent in the art world, so I retired and wrote this down.

Publishing News: Mr. Hu Zhifan, who has worked in the banking industry for ten years, has written a book titled "English Practical Bank Correspondence" based on his experience. It is being sold by the Qunyi Bookstore on Qipan Street. This book covers all types of correspondence required for banking operations, large and small. The Western language is concise and fluent. It is a must-read for students of banking.

Warmth in the Heart (218) Bao Tianxiao 175

Chapter 12: Farewell Banquet, Plucking Flowers to Preserve a Beautiful Image, Elegant Gathering in a Famous Garden, Tea Tasting to Appreciate Beauty

Zuo Shichen thought secretly, "It's not just that the hair should be soft and docile, but the temperament should also be like the hair, soft and docile." Although Ruiyun came from a poor background and experienced hardships, her temper was sometimes not very soft and docile. She was fine with polite people, but once people got close to her, they would inevitably get pricked. It was no big deal to her. Zuo Shichen, holding a pen, urged her, "What dishes do you want to eat? Tell me." Ruiyun said, "You decide for me. Something refreshing. No beef." Zuo Shichen wrote down "Chicken Velvet Pigeon Egg Soup." Then he said, "I remember, you like to eat cold abalone." Ruiyun didn't deny it. He then ordered three more dishes, making a total of five. A Jin said that she only needed three dishes for herself. Zuo Shichen said, "These large dishes are easy to fill up but also easy to get hungry again. Eat your fill first." Zuo Shichen thought, "This meal would be meaningless on ordinary days. They have eaten together several times just for fun. But this time, it can be considered a farewell meal. There won't be another opportunity to treat her to a second meal." Thinking this way, it seemed to have a small meaning. Would her future lead her to heaven or hell? Would she step onto the path of happiness or stumble into the palace of sorrow? This banquet, on the one hand, was like sending off a close friend who had been appointed to a high-ranking official position and was about to take office. On the other hand, it was like a relative being falsely accused and sent to prison, a farewell at the crossroads. But these were all just the fanciful thoughts of a bookworm. The person herself felt nothing. Then, she asked, "Are we not going to perform on stage today? That would be more comfortable." Ruiyun said, "Not only today, but I'm not planning to perform from tomorrow onwards." Before Zuo Shichen could ask the reason, A Jin added, "They came to tell us not to perform." Zuo Shichen asked, "Who is 'they'?" A Jin said, "It's that young master Zhang over there. Their meaning is that it's almost the holiday, so not performing on stage won't be a big loss. The Big Aunt thinks it's best to perform on stage until the day she gets married. Naturally, she just wants to make more money for each performance. But can people agree to her? The news of A Nan getting married has already spread among the guests. She's still performing on stage, and countless rumors are flying around. There are countless people gossiping. We naturally say that there's no such thing, but 'a tightly sealed bottle mouth can't stop the flow of gossip.' How can we hide it from people? Yesterday, the matchmaker of the young master Zhang, Mr. Sun from the pawnshop, came to discuss with the Big Aunt at the business, telling A Nan not to perform on stage anymore. Anyway, it's only two or three days until the holiday." Zuo Shichen said, "That's right. It's already been decided, so why bother with all the work? It's better to rest for a few days. I don't know when they'll come to pick her up after the holiday."

Gold Rush Repeatedly Surges 176

Unprecedented Price of 615 Taels

Another Surge of 8 Taels and 1 Mace to Crush Speculators

Unending Record Peaks Yesterday, the gold price surge was unusually vigorous, hitting a historical high of over 610 taels, causing great fear. The process was smooth, gradually rising with unstoppable momentum. Exchange rates remained unchanged, and domestic rates rose slightly without special progress. Market trading was vigorous, with buyers dominating, leaving speculators speechless. Companies like Yuan Mao Yong, Cheng Feng Yong, and Zhi Feng Yong were among those following. Fu Chang, Yong Feng, and Yuan Cheng Yong had sold, but the transaction volume was not large. The market opened high in the morning and initially fell due to large orders, then softened slightly due to some sales. Later, exchange rates improved and looked upward, jumping to 607 or 608 taels. There was a brief period of consolidation, fluctuating by 3 or 4 taels, but at noon, everything changed. The surge was indescribable, skyrocketing by 10 taels to reach a peak of 615 taels. The possibility of a further decline in silver prices and expensive exchange rates led to large-scale purchases. The recent sales price of Japanese gold by the Japanese bank reached 1 tael 3 mace 7 fen 5 li, and British gold settled at only 5 pence 8125. In the end, the gold price settled at 612 or 613 taels.

The Market Opens With 2 Taels Rise; British Silver Telegraph Declines One-Eighth in Spot, and One-Sixteenth in Forward; Silver Price Decreases Three-Eighths. Gold price for August opened at 606 taels 5 mace, with an increase of 2 taels 1 mace. Spot market had fluctuations of 2 taels. Sellers were active with a soft undercurrent. Japanese gold prices were loose, with Mitsui offering 1 tael 3 mace 5. British gold also advanced to 6 pence 1875. Thus, when the official gold price was announced, it was only 602 taels 2 mace. Also, exchange rates remained unchanged. Soon, smaller dealers took profits and settled their short positions, while Fu Yu and arbitrageurs were also buying. Forward British gold for next month could be done at 6 pence 0625. Hua Bank then sold forward British gold at 6 pence, causing a jump of 5-6 taels, reaching 608 taels 6-7 mace after 10 o'clock.

Momentum Increases Significantly At Noon; News of Exchange Rate Retreat Caused Concern; Spot US Dollar Settled at 36.5 Yuan; British Gold at 5 Pence 9375. With limited buyers on the floor, and with some sellers, price declined over 4 taels, reaching 604 taels after 11 o'clock. Outsiders were coming in to buy, pushing prices up. British Gold was absorbed by banks at 6 pence 0625, buyer interest increased without any selling. The market atmosphere was sharp, breaking through the 610 tael mark. When closing the market it reached 15 taels with most short positions under heavy pressure. Price dropped back 2 taels, then closed at 612 taels 5 mace, with an increase of 8 taels 1 mace compared with the previous day.

Premium Is 60 Taels. Maximum Price in Morning Is 615 Taels, Minimum Price Is 602 Taels 2 Mace, with a difference of 12 Taels 8 Mace. Initial Price Is Still 664 Taels 1 Mace, Then Reduced by Slightly Less Than 60 Taels, Premium in Afternoon Is 52 Taels, Accounting for 611 Taels in July, 13 Taels in August, 11 Taels for Adding Margin. Exchange Rates Tense 177

Yesterday, being Saturday, the foreign exchange market was only open for half a day as usual. The exchange rates posted by HSBC remained unchanged. However, the silver market showed a slight decline. The domestic rates for the three currencies (British, American, and Japanese) were all tense, but not as sharply as the surge in gold prices. The current prices were not far from the posted rates, and arbitrage opportunities became closer. However, the rampant surge in gold prices broke through the 610-tael mark, breaking records repeatedly, even reaching 615 taels. There were fears that prices would continue to rise, with an irresistible momentum. Chinese speculators sold 100,000 pounds sterling to Mitsui Zhengjin Shanghai, and then sold several tens of thousands of pounds more. The rest was bought in by Mitsui. Banks also traded 40,000-50,000 pounds among themselves. Around 100,000 US dollars were traded, with American Bank initially buying and then selling. Various brokers bought several hundred thousand dollars worth of Japanese gold, which was sold by Mitsubishi Mitsui. At the noon closing, the exchange rate for British money decreased by 0.25 compared to the 20th, and US money decreased by half a dollar. Japanese money increased by 1.875. There will be large-scale military equipment settlements in the near future, giving people more peace of mind, making the market more auspicious.

Powerful Rise in Foreign Exchange Rate 179

Continued Rise of 1.75 Cents… Listed Price Once Reached Six Cents

Market Overview: This unexpected surge in the foreign exchange rate has taken everyone by surprise. The continuous upward movement has never retreated. Not only are outsiders astonished, but even those in the industry did not initially anticipate such a sudden surge. It is said that the possibility of foreign exchange rates soaring during this period of abundant banknotes this year was indeed unlikely. However, unforeseen circumstances occurred because banknotes were not issued in large quantities, nor were they shipped to other areas, leading to the widespread use of silver dollars and resulting in this adverse outcome.

Exchange Rate (Foreign Exchange): The market opened with bullish sentiment, and the exchange rate remained strong, closing at 7.22625 cents, up half a cent from the previous morning. Unexpectedly, buying interest surged in the afternoon, and head-end funds became even scarcer. Consequently, the opening price was immediately listed at six cents, but there were no sellers. After a prolonged period of adjustment, the market eventually closed at 7.24 cents, which was 1.375 cents higher than the morning session, resulting in a total increase of about two cents between the two sessions. (Silver Exchange): Dull and unremarkable. The morning session was at 1.2 cents, and the afternoon session was only at 0.6 cents. Head-end withdrawals continued to be high, resulting in a flat market throughout. Bank listings opened at a market rate of five cents.

Subsidiary Coin Market Conditions: The trend of Jiangnan small silver dollars is set. The morning session was at 6.38 cents, and the afternoon session was at 6.37 cents. Fluctuations compared to the previous day were similar. Transactions amounted to 2,000 units in the morning and 1,500 units in the afternoon. Guangdong small silver dollars opened at 5.98 cents, slightly better than the previous afternoon by 0.25 cents. The afternoon session rose with the increase in the exchange rate to 5.9925 cents, up 1.125 cents from the morning. Transactions amounted to 115,000 units in the morning and 15,000 units in the afternoon. Copper coins retracted by 3,000 units, with a wholesale volume of 400,000.

Silver Dollar Inflow and Outflow (Silver): Yesterday was Saturday, and banks closed in the afternoon as usual, resulting in lighter receipts and disbursements. Chinese merchants received and disbursed over 1.8 million, while foreign merchants received and disbursed over 1.5 million, with special disbursements of 1.89 million. Total receipts and disbursements for various goods, foreign exchange taxes, and mortgages amounted to 7.67 million, with 1.3 million withdrawn from warehouses. Japanese banks received and disbursed 2.89 million, with 300,000 deposited in warehouses. Money shops and silver firms received and disbursed over 32 million, with over 3.3 million in head-end receipts and disbursements. Foreign exchange remittances amounted to over 800,000, with about 1 million received in cash. (Foreign Exchange): Foreign exchange drafts amounted to 1.405 million in the morning and 850,000 in the afternoon. There were no banknote transactions in either session. Over-the-counter transactions amounted to 112,000 in the morning and 70,000 in the afternoon. Spot foreign exchange transactions amounted to 320,000 in the morning and 265,000 in the afternoon. Interbank trading amounted to 550,000 in the morning and 600,000 in the afternoon. Foreign exchange receipts and disbursements by various bank accounts were particularly high, totaling over 3 million. Banknote inflows and outflows were only around 1 million. Money shops and foreign exchange firms received and disbursed 6 to 7 million. Head-end foreign exchange receipts and disbursements also increased due to the rising exchange rate, totaling over 5.2 million. Foreign exchange borrowing and lending reached over 2 million. Small money shops traded 400,000 to 500,000.

Miscellaneous Tales of Foreign Exchange Shortage and Rising Rates 180

According to financial circles, rumors of rising exchange rates had already surfaced at the beginning of this week. Therefore, influential financial circles sent letters to the Hangzhou Mint requesting them to start smelting and minting coins. At that time, there was even concern about excessive silver, so large bars of raw silver were shipped to expedite the minting of silver coins. However, recent exports of raw silver from Shanghai have been substantial, resulting in a sudden depletion of reserves. The mint is also experiencing a shortage of raw materials and may have to cease minting. On the other hand, the use of miscellaneous grains is increasing daily. In addition to the shipments made in previous days, another 1.2 million was shipped to the north, 600,000 to Shantou and Xiamen, over 800,000 to the interior, and 1 million to Hankou, totaling over 3.7 to 3.8 million. Furthermore, banks, fearing that the current reserves would be depleted by these large-scale withdrawals, are also trying to collect cash and store it in their vaults as a reserve for banknotes to prevent shortages. This has led to a sudden decrease in the circulating cash supply in the market, creating concerns about insufficient funds for distribution. Moreover, most firms in the industry, believing that silver funds are abundant, have large head-end funds and hold foreign exchange accounts, unwilling to readily sell them off. As a result, a shortage of foreign exchange has been created, and there are fears that there may be significant upward surges in the future.

Cotton Yarn Market in a Brewing State 183

The yarn market is flat and uninteresting, with both sides in a stalemate. Actual sales are sluggish, and the brokers are lifeless due to the impact of the war. Sales are quiet, and the amount of inventory is increasing. Some are already expecting prices to fall, but many are holding tight due to the sharp reduction in exchange rates and the high cost of goods. The price of third-grade yarn is fluctuating sharply, making it increasingly difficult to predict the future of the yarn market.

The market for marked yarn is dull. The market opened with steady foreign cotton prices, but due to the high gold price, retail investors were short, pushing prices up by three to four cents. Litchang bought over 1,000 bales, with other scattered transactions. In the afternoon, there were reports of a sharp drop in third-grade yarn prices, which had reached 111 yuan this month. Sentiment softened slightly, but Maoji bought 1,600 bales, and Dafeng bought 550 bales. Prices for each month fell by 0.1 to 0.2 cents, while this month rose sharply by 0.4 cents. Total transactions for the day were 9,850 bales. The closing prices for marked yarn are recorded below:

Weekly Report on American Cotton Amidst the Sharp Decline 186

Stimulated by Falling Grain and Securities Prices

Cotton Goods Transactions Quiet, New Cotton Good

New York telegram from the 20th reports the cotton market conditions for the past week: The selling pressure on raw cotton this week was stimulated by the weakness of grain and securities market prices. Reports of smooth progress in new cotton production and poor cotton goods trade caused raw cotton prices to fall to new lows for this cotton season. The market price of 12.5 to 13 cents for new cotton futures has attracted more attention, which is evident from inquiries about futures from domestic and foreign cotton mills. These inquiries, coupled with the view that cotton prices have now reached investment levels, have resulted in more attention from brokerage firms. However, most of it is short covering, as it is reported that nighttime temperatures in the cotton belt are quite low, and recent news about cotton production is not very good. However, according to general opinion, cotton production is still satisfactory, but warm and sunny weather is needed now.

Another report says that the cotton market continues to unwind, the reason being good weather, and the securities market and other commodities are also falling in price. At present, the drop may be excessive. However, cotton goods transactions are quiet, spot cotton demand is weak, consumption is not large, and the prospects for new cotton are quite marketable. The Black Market for Japonica Rice is Soaring Uncontrollably 187

Less Than Twenty Vessels in the River

Yesterday, the Shanghai North market felt unprecedented scarcity. Not only were there no goods arriving from the river, but most of the rice boats that had been moored the previous day were turned back. It is said that this was because the price limit was too strict, so they returned to the interior. Another explanation is that they are still at Caojiadu in western Shanghai. As a result, the inventory in the river, including vessels that have been there for more than half a year, is less than twenty. Despite the heavy rain all day, buyers had to purchase to prevent the goods from running out. The price of northern japonica rice soared, and the black market price for top-quality japonica reached around 24 yuan. In total, the price of various grades of japonica rice jumped by more than one yuan. This kind of market is making a record for an unprecedented event. Thin-skinned rice followed suit and rose across the board. There is no accurate market price for each grade. The price for top-quality thin-skinned rice has already been quoted at 20 yuan. All day, there were only transactions, but because of the rain, shipments could not be cleared. The atmosphere in the market was extremely quiet, with no trading on the surface.

In Shanghai South, because of the rain, no goods arrived from the river. Each merchant mainly traded in public association foreign rice. The river rice market here was quiet, and the inventory in the docks was exhausted. Due to the rainy weather, merchants with goods in the warehouses were watching and waiting, with no sales. This situation is unprecedented.

Bean Noodle Market Rose in the Morning, Fell Back in the Afternoon 188

Yesterday, the bean noodle market was active in the morning. Due to the sudden heavy rain, the buying interest of general interior merchants rose again, and the quiet situation of each month returned. Until the market opened in the afternoon, this month carried on the remaining sentiment of the morning. At the highest time, it was again raised to 2 taels, 6 mace, and 1 cent. However, due to factory owners putting more stock on the market, long positions inevitably became wary. In addition, the exchange still strictly limits the date of payment for the certificate, so long positions did not dare to raise prices again, and the market fell back. This month fell by 0.2 cents from the opening price. The forward market fell slightly by 0.1 cents. This month was up by 0.1 cents compared to the previous month. July and August were up by 0.025 cents each. September and October were up by 0.075 cents each. November was unchanged.

Wheat Market Changes Three Times in One Day 189

Yesterday's futures wheat market showed weakness in the morning for each month. Due to factory owners intending to squeeze small long positions, they took the opportunity to sell back, so this month fell to 4 taels, 9 mace, and 6 cents at the lowest, July to 4 taels, 9 mace, and 9 cents. The remaining months had fewer ups and downs. Until the market opened in the afternoon, the bean noodle market turned bullish, and interior merchants purchased very smoothly, so the near and forward market became bullish significantly. However, later, because long positions sold back, the market turned soft again. Looking ahead, if the weather clears up and the arrival of goods becomes smooth, the market may loosen up a little. As a result, this month was down 0.02 cents compared to the previous day, July was up 0.1 cents, August was up 0.2 cents, September was up 0.3 cents, and October was up 0.4 cents, November was up 0.3 cents. Now, Fuxin is unchanged, and the market situation is slightly flat. Seafood: New Dried Shrimp Rose by More Than 3 Taels 191

Due to the sudden cold weather, the output of new dried shrimp has been greatly reduced. According to reports from water brokers in Ningbo, the most that fishing boats have caught near the shore recently is only 2,000 to 3,000 catties, and as little as 1,000 to 700 catties. Therefore, fishermen are unwilling to sell cheaply, leading to a gradual increase in the market price to 33 yuan. Because the production price has risen in Shanghai, and the Shantou brokers have been actively selling recently, the previous goods have been sold out, and the cost of future purchases will be around 28 taels. Therefore, the sales price of the firms has also risen in unison, with the market price yesterday being 26 taels, which is very bullish.

Metals: Metals Affected by the Plum Rain 192

The plum rain season is affecting the metal market. Although export brokers have recently added a lot of goods, they are afraid of getting wet and mildew, so they are waiting for the weather to clear before loading ships and sending cars. The purchasers are therefore stopping purchases due to this relationship. The market transaction is greatly reduced, and the trend is extremely calm. Yesterday, in addition to a few kinds of transactions such as French West nails, cement, bamboo steel, new lead wire, etc., there is nothing to record for large transactions.

Qingfeng Garden

Vanguard Weekly Launches First Issue 194

Published on June 22

Vanguard Weekly, edited by the Vanguard Society, contains various new literature criticism and discussion. The first issue was published on June 22. The main contents include "The Decline of Chinese Literature and Art," "Nationalist Literature and Art," "Talks," etc. "Talks" includes articles such as "Mr. Lu Xun's Vision," "The So-Called Slaves of Doctrine," and "Charms and Wizards." The price per issue is 2 cents. Major bookstores in this city, such as Kaiming, Zhenmeishan, Jinwu, Jiangwan Fuxin Bookstore, and various newspaper vendors, all sell it.

Central University's Bi-Monthly Publication 195

Indeed, the spirit of a school and the way it studies and develops depends on what comes out of that school. Since the publication of Central University's bi-monthly publication, the entire university suddenly emitted a life-giving light. In the previously stagnant "academic institution," this point of "the great atmosphere of academic institution" has now been warmed and transformed.

I remember when it (referring to the bi-monthly publication) was not yet born, someone came to visit our school and said, "The dead aspects of your university have a clear overview in the Central University, but the living aspects of your university only have future scholars with silver medals inscribed with 'Striving for Perfection,' and nothing else." At that time, I felt a subtle pain in my heart when I heard these words.

Now, thankfully, the bi-monthly publication has been declared to have come into existence with a clap of thunder. This is certainly something we should celebrate at the beginning, but at the same time, the words of outsiders criticizing our school have gradually lost their authenticity.

But what is the content of Central University's bi-monthly publication like? This is what outsiders want to hear most. Although the content itself can explain it, I would like to say a few words here. Its content is divided into seven sections: dissertations, research, translation, weekly review, literature and art, miscellaneous works, and news. Its purpose is to introduce world scholarship, develop the research results of teachers and students at Central University, and spread the progress of Central University. In December of last year, the school authorities published a special literary issue, increased the number of pages, and enriched the content, resulting in deep praise from general readers.

The 16th issue has recently been published. (Xian Rong)

Central Institute of Technology

Preparing to Publish the Journal of Engineering 196

The Central Institute of Technology, which is responsible for leading the nation's engineering academic affairs, has long thought of publishing a journal of engineering to publish discussions and works, and to introduce new knowledge, so as to promote construction and improve academic standards. However, due to the lack of funding for publishing, it has not been possible to proceed. Recently, seeing that the Department of Earth Sciences has published a journal of geography, its influence has not only made students specializing in the study of geography feel a deep interest in this subject, but also many students from other departments have increased their common knowledge of geography due to the introduction of the journal. Therefore, the teachers and students of the Institute of Technology feel that the previous publishing requirement is even more urgent, and have specifically requested the school to allocate funds for the publication of the Journal of Engineering. The content of the journal is divided into seven sections: illustrations, commentaries, writings, translations, investigations, industrial news, and appendices. (Xian Rong)

Shanghai Market

Market News 197

The Prosperity Real Estate Company at No. 50 Nanjing Road announces that the company publishes a Shanghai Real Estate Monthly every month. The June issue has now been published, containing a very detailed report on the real estate market conditions in May. The relationship between exchange rates and real estate is discussed in particular detail, making it essential reading for those who wish to know about the Shanghai real estate situation. Furthermore, this is a free publication; simply send a letter to request a copy, it says.

The Guanghua Printing Company at the end of East Huade Road in Shanghai announces that since the launch of its Pocket Bookkeeping, it has been very well received by all sectors. Recently, it has been revised again and changed to a loose-leaf style, with an extremely exquisite spring binder shell. The content has been further improved, making it more convenient to use. The whole set sells for two silver dollars. Additional account tables are available at half a dollar per bundle. The general distribution point is at Wang Yun Li Kou in the Qiuqiu Chang, telephone number 15592.

The Yanhua Restaurant, opposite the Dankui Stage No. 1 on Fourth Road, announces that the restaurant has now added various set menus, ranging from two to five yuan. The taste is naturally delicious, the dishes are exceptionally abundant, and the cuisine is particularly exquisite. These set menus are a token of appreciation for the patronage of all sectors over the years. The restaurant does not seek high profits, but aims to become famous. Patrons, please take note. The restaurant has also added a summer cold drink section, offering items such as Beautiful Lady Ice Cream and frozen fruits, all of which are fully available, it says.

The Qingyise Restaurant at the intersection of Third Road and Zhejiang Road announces that the newly hired chef, Mr. Luo, has been studying Cantonese cuisine for more than thirty years. His cooking is excellent, and the flavor is exquisite, truly possessing the legacy of Yi Ya. Therefore, since he took office, the restaurant has been packed every day, with no empty seats in the evening. Business is once again booming. As the weather is getting warmer, more attention is being paid to food. All utensils used are washed with boiling water before use, striving for cleanliness and hygiene. Various summer cold drinks are also available, such as American ice cream in three flavors: vanilla, cream, and fruit, as well as frozen fruits such as lychees, pineapples, cherries, and loquats. Prices are all extremely low. Therefore, although it has been raining continuously recently, there are still many diners, it says.

The Xieshen Paper Money Company in Guanqun Fang, west of the Qiuqiu Chang on Nanjing Road, announces that the company's various brands of paper money, money orders, and treasury bond papers are famous at the time. Now, a large shipment of No. 1, 2, and 3 paper money paper has arrived directly from the Globe Brand Paper Factory. The goods are genuine, and the prices are fair, satisfying all purchasers. The company also sells plate-making chemicals and materials, such as Luo Dian red powder, yellow powder, black powder, anthracite, copper plates, and zinc plates. However, the stock of these items is limited, so purchasers should act quickly, it says.

The Dajicheng Leather Goods Bureau at the corner of Henan Road and Jiujiang Road announces that since its rise in Shanghai the year before last, it has gathered fox furs of beautiful quality and exquisite craftsmanship, constantly innovating and establishing a unique style, which has long been praised by people in Shanghai as the king of the fur industry. Recently, the bureau has taken advantage of the summer slack season to establish a summer cloth and straw hat department, procuring the latest 1930s styles of men's and women's gold silk straw hats from overseas, as well as summer cloth, a famous product of Liuyang, Sichuan. The straw hats are fashionable in style and elegant in decoration, and this is the first time they have arrived in Shanghai, exclusively sold by the bureau. The summer cloth is soft and does not wrinkle easily. There is also a kind of mosquito net summer cloth, which is cool and breathable, and more durable than gauze or bamboo cloth. To give preferential treatment to customers, the bureau is partially fulfilling its obligations, selling both retail and wholesale at the same price, which is uniformly low, unlike those who specialize in this business.

Page 26

They are now displayed in the internal display windows, welcoming all sectors to come and choose for comparison, it says.

Theater News 198

The Haixing Film Company announces that the company was founded by prominent Shanghai merchants Li Zhongyue, Tang Weiyu, Zhu Mingqian, Dong Tianduo, and others. The first film produced is "Times and Heroes," written by the author Huang Tianduo. It is Dong's most powerful masterpiece. The plot is tragic and tortuous, passionate and慷慨, and full of the intense emotions of a stormy sea, and the courageous spirit of lightning劈雷. The story of romance between men and women, and the world of bandits and beauties, is even more moving. The company, appreciating the preciousness of this drama, has spared no effort and financial resources to produce a martial arts love epic that is melancholy and glamorous, and worthy of song and tears. Currently, costumes and props are being custom-made, and actors with artistic talent in the country are being selected to play the main roles. A huge filming location is being built in western Shanghai. As soon as everything is ready, filming will begin. It is heard that they will first go to Langshan, Tongzhou to take exterior shots. The success of this film will undoubtedly add color to the screen and is truly unprecedented good news in domestic films, it says.
